	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Mario Vargas Llosa</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article uses <a href="/wiki/Spanish_naming_customs" title="Spanish naming customs">Spanish naming customs</a>: the first or paternal <a href="/wiki/Surname" title="Surname">family name</a> is <i><b>Vargas</b></i>&#32;and the second or maternal family name is <i><b>Llosa</b></i>.</div>

<p><b>Jorge Mario Pedro Vargas Llosa, 1st Marquess of Vargas Llosa</b> (born March 28, 1936), more commonly known as <b>Mario Vargas Llosa</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/ɑːr/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;far&#39;">ɑːr</span><span title="/ɡ/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/j/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;yes&#39;">j</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[ˈmaɾjo ˈβaɾɣaz ˈʎosa]</a></span>), is a Peruvian writer, politician, journalist, essayist and college professor. Vargas Llosa is one of Latin America's most significant novelists and essayists, and one of the leading writers of his generation. Some critics consider him to have had a larger international impact and worldwide audience than any other writer of the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Boom" title="Latin American Boom">Latin American Boom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 he won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>, "for his cartography of structures of power and his trenchant images of the individual's resistance, revolt, and defeat."<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Vargas Llosa rose to international fame in the 1960s with novels such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Time_of_the_Hero" title="The Time of the Hero">The Time of the Hero</a></i> (<i>La ciudad y los perros</i>, literally <i>The City and the Dogs</i>, 1963/1966<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Green_House" title="The Green House">The Green House</a></i> (<i>La casa verde</i>, 1965/1968), and the monumental <i><a href="/wiki/Conversation_in_the_Cathedral" title="Conversation in the Cathedral">Conversation in the Cathedral</a></i> (<i>Conversación en la catedral</i>, 1969/1975). He writes prolifically across an array of <a href="/wiki/Literary_genre" title="Literary genre">literary genres</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Literary_criticism" title="Literary criticism">literary criticism</a> and journalism. His novels include comedies, murder mysteries, historical novels, and political thrillers. Several, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_Pantoja_and_the_Special_Service" title="Captain Pantoja and the Special Service">Captain Pantoja and the Special Service</a></i> (1973/1978) and <i><a href="/wiki/Aunt_Julia_and_the_Scriptwriter" title="Aunt Julia and the Scriptwriter">Aunt Julia and the Scriptwriter</a></i> (1977/1982), have been adapted as feature films.
</p><p>Many of Vargas Llosa's works are influenced by the writer's perception of <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peruvian</a> society and his own experiences as a native Peruvian. Increasingly, however, he has expanded his range, and tackled themes that arise from other parts of the world. In his essays, Vargas Llosa has made many criticisms of nationalism in different parts of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Kordi_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kordi-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Another change over the course of his career has been a shift from a style and approach associated with <a href="/wiki/Modernist_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist literature">literary modernism</a>, to a sometimes playful <a href="/wiki/Postmodernism" title="Postmodernism">postmodernism</a>.
</p><p>Like many Latin American writers, Vargas Llosa has been politically active throughout his career; over the course of his life, he has gradually moved from the <a href="/wiki/Political_left" class="mw-redirect" title="Political left">political left</a> towards more right-wing <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberalism</a>. While he initially supported the Cuban revolutionary government of <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>, Vargas Llosa later became disenchanted with its policies, particularly after the imprisonment of Cuban poet <a href="/wiki/Heberto_Padilla" title="Heberto Padilla">Heberto Padilla</a> in 1971. He ran for the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Peru" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Peru">Peruvian presidency</a> in <a href="/wiki/1990_Peruvian_general_election" title="1990 Peruvian general election">1990</a> with the center-right <i><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Front_(Peru)" title="Democratic Front (Peru)">Frente Democrático</a></i> coalition, advocating <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">classical liberal</a> reforms, but lost the election to <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Fujimori" title="Alberto Fujimori">Alberto Fujimori</a>. He is the person who, in 1990, "coined the phrase that circled the globe,"<sup id="cite_ref-terra_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terra-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> declaring on Mexican television, "Mexico is the perfect dictatorship," a statement which became an adage during the following decade.
</p>
